<rating>5<//rating><Review>Lovely little coffee shop in Scott's Valley with delicious coffee, delightful pastries, and friendly baristas. They knew their regulars well, which is always a good sign. They had a lot of food too, not just coffee. They serve Lulu Carpenter's coffee here, which I had never had before, and their espresso was very nice, bright, bold, with a hint of berry (to my taste buds at least).

My wife loved her latte with whole milk, which she usually sweetens but didn't and still really enjoyed. Her breakfast bagel was also very good. My cappuccino was bright, the espresso strong, and the oat milk (Oatly Barista) paired well with it. I also ate a Lemon poppyseed with lemon curd muffin which was really nice and moist. Such a lovely way to start the day.

Highly recommend checking it out. Plenty of outdoor seating too. Followed all Covid guidelines.< /Review><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMMGh2q3VloURmobFiUUHLdVHBrk2FJD4afOjpU=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipM57_ER8s9NnA2ZQOGEFO2QMTQNfe6glzoqPNtS=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNJLq193M2R-mIg3FYU8D90II2GTxF-RY4ohss-=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /Pics>< Resp>

<username>Vitaliy Khomyak</username><Response>None< /Response>< Review>
I Love Coffee!!

So driving to Santa Cruz and had a craving for coffee so yelped this place and seemed like great reviews. Decided to check it out. Parking out side was a breeze. Plenty of parking available. Walking in the store has a nice coffee smell. Everything in the shop looks clean and professional and organized. Felt like a homey coffee shop.

There was a group of 7 of us and we all got our own special coffee. For the 7 of us the barista did a very fast and accurate job and even made foam prints on our lattes (unfortunately forgot to take a picture). I personally got the coconut syrup hot latte and my fianc√© got the same thing but iced. The quality of the drink was acceptable.

1 small downside.  Not sure if they don't provide it or if they just didn't have any when we were there but they didn't have any hot cup sleeves. When I asked she kindly offered a second cup which was nice.

Overall expensive was definitely a 5 Star. And if I ever catch myself in this area again. Will be coming back<//Review>

<rate>4</rate>< text>
Fast and friendly service. Clean interior. Tasty food and most importantly well made espresso and espresso drinks. Coffee Cat is part of Lulu Carpenter's, a long-standing local company which has several cafes in Santa Cruz. In my experience they have been making excellent coffee for decades. Their shops may not be as big or modern as some third-wave cafes but the coffee is just as good...and perhaps a bit less expensive as well. If you're headed in or out of Santa Cruz and want good coffee off of Highway 17 check out Coffee Cat.<//text>

<Name>Scott Berry< /Name><Time>1489584564389<//Time>< Rating>
5< /Rating>
< Review>
I sadly misjudged Coffee Cat for many months and titled my nose as I drove past to visit Starbucks and Peet's for my regular coffee & work sessions. But thankfully the coffee gods did not give up on me and recently guided my vehicle to Coffee Cat.

Boy have I been missing out! Upon walking in I was excited to see a very spacious seating area with nice wood tables and way less people than the other big-name coffee shops. They even have power outlets along the entire wall for all those seated along it - amazing! The wifi is also very good and the bathrooms are decently clean.

And to my even greater surprise, they have a Clover!! I love coffee pulled from a Clover, always my first choice if available which is rare. Their other coffee selections are also very good and the ladies really know what they are doing behind the counter. They also have a great food selection with healthy, authentic ingredients. And if that isn't enough, Safeway is right next door - very convenient.

Overall, I am very impressed with Coffee Cat and have directed all of my coffee funds and work sessions here. Thank you CC!</Review>

I told her I was a student and could present her my student ID as a form of state identification, to which she went back to talk to the manager. They both denied me of my free-trial pass, but said that they could sign me up for a membership instead. <Text>One thing I really hate about this gym is the steam room closing at 11:30 pm. They have a sign that says 11 pm to 4 am as it actually requires 5 hours to clean the steam room. It doesn't. This is clearly a ploy for them to conserve energy and save money during the least utilized time of the gym. If you ask the employees at the front counter, they will tell you the steam room and sauna is 24 hours. It's not. Fortunately, the sauna will stay warm until 3 am even despite being turned off because heat can be sustained longer than steam. The purpose of the steam room is for therapeutic muscle recovery and it works far more effectively than a sauna. So, last Friday, I was bummed out because I was told by the front counter that it stop operating at midnight. I got in at 11:40 pm after rushing my workout to beat the midnight time, but it was already too late. 11:30 pm is the correct time. Never did I think I would have to rush my workout at a 24-HOUR gym. The steam room use to turn off around 2-3 am circa 2016 but they have cut it down by a few hours (anyway they can cut costs). If enough people complain, of course the corporate office would reinstate that 2-3 am turnoff time. This is becoming the norm for many 24hr gyms in San Diego, not discrimative to College Grove. So, it's very frustrating for members like me who value the steam rooms for greater recovery. Other than that, this gym is great.< /Text><pics>None< /pics>< resp>

< userid>
103863953257262594662< /userid>
< Review>
Awesome service. I found a bubble in my tire sidewall (after it unexpectedly kissed the curb) on a Thursday late afternoon (4-5ish) and called the shops around my area. America's Tire was busy (took a total of three call and ~15 minute wait to speak with someone), and similarly no one picked up at the nearby Pep Boys. Both suggested I come in early Friday as a walk-in.

I called Mac's auto and was given a price estimate immediately, and they were willing to see me ASAP. I dropped my car off in the evening (per my request) and received a call from them first thing in the morning to give me an update.

The general rule of thumb is to change tires in pairs due to uneven wear, and most shops I've been to really push me to change the pair. However, Mac's let me know just for my knowledge, but presented my options - swap only one tire now, or swap both and keep the used tire as a spare. I asked some questions about wear and decided to swap just the one, which they accepted without hassle.

The repair took less than a day (without reservation) and the total including alignment, was very reasonable - definitely cheaper than what America's Tire in Culver had charged me earlier this year, comparatively.

The people were all super friendly and I was in the shop for less than 15 minutes total from start to finish.

I definitely plan on taking my car back in as long as I'm in the OC area!<//Review>

<review>The walking tours were some of the best experiences my wife and I had on our trips to SF.  A friend had recommended the Walking Chinese Food Tour, which is the first one we took.  It was fantastic visiting the shops and seeing how fortune cookies were made.  Please keep in mind this is a walking tour and the China Town area has lots of hills.  Although the group doesn't move along at a sprint, it does need to keep moving in order to see everything within the time window.  Wear comfortable clothes and walking/jogging shoes.  As my wife put it, don't worry about looking cute on this tour.

The following year, we took the tour of Little Italy.  It was a lot of fun!  We enjoyed the bakeries, the culture and the fresh roasted coffee, which is the best cup I've ever had!  This tour didn't have as many hills as the China Town tour and it moved at a bit slower pace.  Be prepared to eat A LOT!!  We had made reservations to eat at an Italian restaurant at the end of the tour and had to cancel because we weren't hungry at all.

The City offers a ton of different sights to be seen, but the best ones that we've experienced were these walking tours.  We always recommend these to anyone visiting SF who haven't already done them.  Enjoy!</review><pictures>None</pictures>< Resp>

<text>The Local Tastes tour was a delightful way to learn about San Francisco's Chinatown and experience it first-hand!  From the time our guide met us at the entrance gate and began explaining the symbolism of our surroundings, we felt transported back to an earlier time.  We walked at a leisurely pace and listened to a fascinating historical narrative between tastings, which included multiple restaurants, a tea room, open-air market and a fortune cookie factory.  The quantity of food was generous and in fact more than we could eat - so we took the leftovers with us for an afternoon snack!  The entire experience was a very good value for the cost and left us completely satisfied and wanting to find similar tours in other cities.< /text></record></dataset><record>

< Text>
I attended this tour twice, once two years ago and the last time was about a year ago. I would have to say I really enjoyed the first tour better, we had the same tour guide Tom, I think his name was? However, we stopped at more places on the first tour, maybe it was the time of the year, I'm not sure, but it was just so much better the first time. We were able to eat fish tacos, taste authentic coffee, go to a bakery and taste fresh bread, we even went to an Italian joint where we sampled fresh dishes, it was delish! And the walk wasn't hard, it was all relatively close proximity to everything. It was very easy meeting up for the tour and we ended at the same spot and enjoyed our last dish, pizza. This is where we said our goodbye's and was given an Ipad in case we wanted to leave a tip. On the second tour, I must say it was extremely easy to book as I called the same day an arranged our reservations over the phone with Tom. Anyways, if your passing through or have sometime I would recommend this tour, it was fun!</Text>

< text>
I was looking for hard to find plumbing shut off valves and Reds Plumbing was recommended.
It was easy enough to find but there is no parking except for around the corner. The store itself shows signs of aging.
When I first walked in there seemed to be a  lot of plumbing needs from sinks and toilets to faucets and valves. Other reviews weren't off when describing this place with years of dust covering what I think were display sinks and fixtures. It seemed very cluttered and unorganized to me but as long as the clerks knew where everything was then that's okay with me.
The clerk was helpful but didn't carry any of the items I was looking for.
For a neighborhood store I guess this shop would fill my needs but for special older homes it didn't meet my needs.</text>

< Review>
Yes Hello. I am a master plumber and have been to Reds many times. In reviewing the comments made before this one, I can see why the customers had problems. Reds usually deals with the more professional plumbers who know the correct terms for the supplies they need. While the people who wrote their comments were sincere in their beliefs, the terms they used to request the plumbling supplies they needed were not the correct or right names they were trying to get. The term "coupler" for instance is very vague. There are several types of "couplings" in the plumbing industry, but none are called couplers.Then there is the issue of the materials they are made from. For instance, were you seeking copper, galvanized iron, black gas pipe, plastic PVC pipe, ext? As for the person who wanted the "1/2 inch nipple adapters or 1/2 inch nipple connecters", same again, adapt to what, Iron pipe, copper, adapt to a larger or smaller size? If you are not a professional, then the best way to get what you need from a supply store is to take a photo of it, or take the part to the store and show them what you need. We all live and learn. I hope this has helped you understand a complicated industry.</Review>

< Review>
YUM!!  Thiswas the first time we had eaten inside a restaurant since March, 2020.  It was after 3 PM and we each ordered an entree.  The coastal linguine was a bit too garlicky for me.  Husband ordered roast beef atop mashed potatoes.  He originally was going to order the coastal linguine so when I suggested swapping, he readily agreed.  We enjoyed both entrees although we both agreed to ask for light garlic on the linguine if we were to order it again.  As is our custom, we ordered one dessert and 2 spoons.  It was the pumpkin creme brulee.  Sadly it wasn't quite up to par.  We would have enjoyed a stronger pumpkin flavor.  It was more like a pudding, with no whipped cream.  The staff was attentive...personable and very friendly.  The restaurant was one of the older ones but simply decorated and very clean (which is probably the most important attribute in today's world!)  Would we dine there again?  Yes we would.<//Review>
